          <div class="date-outer">
        
<h2 class='date-header'><span>Thursday, January 12, 2012</span></h2>

          <div class="date-posts">
        
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post hentry'>
<a name='5744146941346663756'></a>
<h3 class='post-title entry-title'>
<a href='https://contagiodump.blogspot.com/2012/01/blackhole-ramnit-samples-and-analysis.html'>Blackhole Ramnit - samples and analysis</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body entry-content'>
<div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
<div style="text-align: left;">
<br />
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivO05eQpmPcwSD66bksBA8gbHWG33vja5q_U4Ccd3f7M3kmZqlsqUrcjLi5bSlGU0k0LU4u8MwYRYTJu7dD7kgkt8ikbGZxoye_5bTJUgKW5XX_zMRiP0Y6ca-xlTV6MsmctNicnqNJVk/s1600/bsod1.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivO05eQpmPcwSD66bksBA8gbHWG33vja5q_U4Ccd3f7M3kmZqlsqUrcjLi5bSlGU0k0LU4u8MwYRYTJu7dD7kgkt8ikbGZxoye_5bTJUgKW5XX_zMRiP0Y6ca-xlTV6MsmctNicnqNJVk/s1600/bsod1.gif" /></a></div>
Ramnit - a Zeus-like trojan/worm/file infector with rootkit capabilities has been in the wild for a long time but recently made news because <a href="http://blog.seculert.com/2012/01/ramnit-goes-social.html">Seculert reported about a financial variant of this malware aimed at stealing Facebook credentials. </a><br />
<br />
While I did not see any Facebook related activity in my samples, I am posting them anyway for your research as their functionality is the same.<br />
<br />
The samples I have are being spread not via Facebook but via Blackhole exploit kit, which is a very effective method. Blackhole exploit kit was associated with the spread of ZeuS, Spyeye, and it is not surprising that Ramnit is being spread in the same manner by the same groups. The group of command and control servers that I researched is associated with pharma spam and "Canadian" online pharmacies.<br />
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjWM53fLnTGNIKIoeAKSHYbFvh7rXiSotaeAP8oyVsghpdOlonTuz7RAlZ-mtw6nAgt74OaxS7uupIArauxs83lrdf4xK06mCc5MB3RvydKBphyME3u-exD0xGyj1BPRnQfBJwj0YgqAeU/s1600/bsod1.gif" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><br /></a><br />
<br />
<a name='more'></a><div style="text-align: left;">
<br />
<div class="date-posts">
<div class="post-outer">
<div class="post hentry">
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
</div>

<br />
<h3 style="background-color: #618f2b; color: white; text-align: center;">










<span style="font-weight: bold;"><span style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS',sans-serif; font-size: large;"><span style="font-family: 'Courier New',Courier,monospace;">Distribution</span></span></span></h3>
The files analysed were / are being distributed via Blackhole exploit pack. It starts with the usual large letter message "Please wait page is loading" -then Java exploit launches and compromise takes place if the machine is vulnerable. . Here you can see the Blackhole domains spreading Ramnit in the Malwaredomainlist . <b>Amberfreda.com</b> domain belongs to a legitimate company and is registered in Arizona, while a subdomain <b><span style="color: #38761d;"><span style="color: red;">best</span><span style="color: black;">.amberfreda.com</span></span></b> is registered by some Ukranian guy. Not sure how they managed that.<br />

<br />
<h3 style="background-color: #618f2b; color: white; text-align: center;">















<span style="font-weight: bold;"><span style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS',sans-serif; font-size: large;"><span style="font-family: 'Courier New',Courier,monospace;">Brief Analysis</span></span></span></h3>
<b>&nbsp;607B2219FBCFBFE8E6AC9D7F3FB8D50E</b><br />
&nbsp;Hendrik Adrian from Japan posted his analysis of the same sample<a href="http://translate.google.com/translate?sl=ja&amp;tl=en&amp;js=n&amp;prev=_t&amp;hl=en&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;layout=2&amp;eotf=1&amp;u=http%3A%2F%2Funixfreaxjp.blogspot.com%2F2012%2F01%2Framnit.html&amp;act=url"> ( 0day.JP - Ramnit) </a>where he described the files created by the malware and&nbsp; the spam sending capabilities of the bot .<br />
<br />
<div style="text-align: left;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg56u2YOy38IXqQcIJoHh_-OU418LGz01GY2eEcb0V2Gxtd1GOOwpK5JJWwYMzcKyq7rs3IpHEQMxcT-GTElx0tKdEXhZ5KvWP1AW1yILk7HXCeueuElC2BVjGcHcd6f4DhImzVYFniaaI/s1600/bsod.GIF" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="145" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg56u2YOy38IXqQcIJoHh_-OU418LGz01GY2eEcb0V2Gxtd1GOOwpK5JJWwYMzcKyq7rs3IpHEQMxcT-GTElx0tKdEXhZ5KvWP1AW1yILk7HXCeueuElC2BVjGcHcd6f4DhImzVYFniaaI/s320/bsod.GIF" width="320" /></a>The bot deletes registry settings for the safe boot, which causes BSOD and prevents one from removing the malicious files in the safe mode.</div>
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh68qLYzap2LMME5SFlPi1UoyGTH6HSaPMrzOtKiRQULHsuWcOoVY_C-DVjOiPrPEk9SuEg9dANmIy2texum3yX6BFvdx1MRdvOIrY7z6tlS_JANyxazrS-seZZbJPUkKkFFMnn68jpHtM/s1600/bsod1.gif" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"></a></div>

<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9d5FwXfCkgfnx4TlhdMZZkDr5-Pr2enQA6SD3LNnxi5tn2tz5bnN4urO5cbPnYmQwg2IdbYB3BnpPmBnPRVhUfTK_LGVXLVPD4lqaSvrtj1z2MqnjLmI2sJI-2M7HYYagmp4WOr5Wk_w/s1600/handles.GIF" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9d5FwXfCkgfnx4TlhdMZZkDr5-Pr2enQA6SD3LNnxi5tn2tz5bnN4urO5cbPnYmQwg2IdbYB3BnpPmBnPRVhUfTK_LGVXLVPD4lqaSvrtj1z2MqnjLmI2sJI-2M7HYYagmp4WOr5Wk_w/s1600/handles.GIF" /></a></div>
<br />
&nbsp;Ramnit injects itself into two&nbsp; svchost.exe processes and you&nbsp; can see them if you sort all processes by PID, the last two will those created by Ramnit.<br />
<br />
&nbsp;It generates spam that it sends out on port 25,<a href="http://translate.google.com/translate?sl=ja&amp;tl=en&amp;js=n&amp;prev=_t&amp;hl=en&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;layout=2&amp;eotf=1&amp;u=http%3A%2F%2Funixfreaxjp.blogspot.com%2F2012%2F01%2Framnit.html&amp;act=url"> Hendrik already described this behavior in his post.</a><br />
<br />
<b>C33E7ED929760020820E8808289C240E</b><br />
<div style="text-align: left;">
&nbsp;The second file has file infector features I did not observe in<b> 607B2219FBCFBFE8E6AC9D7F3FB8D50E.</b></div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
As you see in the log below, malicious svchost.exe modifies or tries to modify every binary and HTML file by appending malicious code to each file or a vbs script to HTML files &nbsp; -&nbsp; like described in this post by ESET <a href="http://www.eset.eu/encyclopaedia/win32-ramnit-a-backdoor-ircnite-bwy-w32?lng=en">Win32/Ramnit.A.</a> and here in the post by Avira&nbsp; - <a href="http://techblog.avira.com/2010/11/25/closer-look-at-w32ramnit-c/en/">Closer look at W32/Ramnit.C</a></div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
<br />
This does not break the infected binaries, all files continue to work as designed, except they infect or reinfect the computer they are running on. Webmasters may upload infected html files and visitors of their sites may get infected as well. For an average user, it is impossible to clean a system compromised with Ramnit file injector and use it confidence. The only way is say good bye to all the HTM(L), DLL and EXE files and build a new system without trying to copy any hrml files, bookmark or applications.</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
<br /></div>

<h3 style="background-color: #618f2b; color: white; font-weight: normal; text-align: center;">










<b><span style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS',sans-serif; font-size: large;"><span style="font-family: 'Courier New',Courier,monospace;">Traffic</span></span></b></h3>
<b>607B2219FBCFBFE8E6AC9D7F3FB8D50E - C&amp;C is sinkholed</b><b>C33E7ED929760020820E8808289C240E&nbsp; - C&amp;C is active</b><br />
<br />
<div style="text-align: left;">
Despite the fact that the C&amp;C for 607B2219FBCFBFE8E6AC9D7F3FB8D50E is sinkholed, it is still interesting to see the malware behavior when it tries to establish a connection with the server.</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
<br />
Ramnit samples used by the same group of attackers have overlapping set of C&amp;C servers - the list is not the same but I found that my samples that are supposedly later version that Ramnit.AK have approximately 80% overlap in C&amp;C list used by this RamnitAK binary <a href="http://www.sophos.com/en-us/threat-center/threat-analyses/viruses-and-spyware/Troj%7ERamnit-AK.aspx">described by Sophos </a>.&nbsp; I have combined the two lists and ran WHOIS queries to establish active C&amp;C and their location and registration.</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
<br /></div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
The communications with the sinkholed server below show that once the bot receives SYN command from the C&amp;C, it sends <b>6 bytes of data.</b> Exact same behavior is described in this analysis of&nbsp; the binaries from Summer 2011&nbsp; - with the only difference that the second packet sent by the bot was not 75 bytes but 149 bytes <a href="http://www.emergingthreatspro.com/bot-of-the-day/bot-of-the-day-ramnitninmul/">Bot of the Day: Ramnit/NinmulMonday, July 18th, 2011</a>. If connection with the server is established, the traffic continues on on port 443, it is encoded but it is not SSL, it is some sort of custom protocol. <a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjSOsf2y4sxjHB_mjymLvIWmVFhssHHdTnS8litz9wV7tSnr-lvLkMj_Xxyb8rf2YvfGNp4o_TyTWq2ABKMlrm87ELGx5-MG5NWySyALhoNt45pDesMxJ7ZzZIiOTSSr2dbzkTY6G3d3T0/s1600/6b.GIF" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="156" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjSOsf2y4sxjHB_mjymLvIWmVFhssHHdTnS8litz9wV7tSnr-lvLkMj_Xxyb8rf2YvfGNp4o_TyTWq2ABKMlrm87ELGx5-MG5NWySyALhoNt45pDesMxJ7ZzZIiOTSSr2dbzkTY6G3d3T0/s640/6b.GIF" width="640" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi6hDK2PSFwRoTiVhbEPh810z-xPo1ldliRzDXUDGMFEdbSLLErowcAVgrWqu7QlDxRg_UKgfsIf49tdSS-_XTcXNdNxOuQe9TGfjoQPO3abd50fMob_VTZjPaNhe0KCa8vHaXgT-05n5g/s1600/6b.GIF" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><br /></a><br />
<div style="text-align: left;">
The bot is going through the list of domains trying to find those that are active. Most of the domains are not registered yet but the two currently active domains were registered on<b> January 5 and 6, 2011. </b>It appears that the attackers register new domains as soon as the lose any due to sinkholing and domain cancellations. Since all the domains have the most random names, they are not likely to be registered by someone else before they are needed. Having each binary to check a long list of domains makes the bot very noisy (consider making IDS signatures based on UDP port 53 thresholds) but it prevents the death of the botnet in case of the C&amp;C loss. I have complied a list of approximately 400 domains with only 21 of them registered.&nbsp;&nbsp; If you created DNS blocks or sinkhole domains, consider blocking or sinkholing all of them, not only active.</div>

<h2 class='title'>About contagio</h2>
<div class='widget-content'>
Contagio is a collection of the historic malware samples, threats, observations, and analyses.<p></p>
<div style="display: flex; align-items: center;">
  <img src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEieKJB9iR6r5eAoodbA436bn8bvNdqGGqtMdUxeCz8BQ2OUkOqMPPjigFgbuG9J0Q4VTraqwm4uT-fZ--Fcbswum1s2H7F6-lmZN2oqT51VHA6NziTxCaIfNCaXBAQQ80BvDJT1zNHONhsTaKRI_AjnYg6kORfoAlunUylRHoWiapLkUxBSeoa-rTzY/s618/NoPutler.png" alt="No Putler" width="70" height="70" style="float: left; margin: 0 10px 10px 0;" />
  <div>

    <p>Malware samples are available for download by any responsible whitehat researcher. </p>
  </div>
</div> 
By downloading the samples, anyone waives all rights to claim punitive, incidental and consequential damages resulting from mishandling or self--infection
   <p><span style="font-style: italic;">If you see errors, typos, etc, please let me know.</span></p>
</div>
<div class='clear'></div>
</div><div class='widget HTML' data-version='1' id='HTML9'>
